This simplifies to: $g(x) \geq \lceil \frac{x^2 + 1}{2} \rceil$ for all x. **Checking if we can achieve the lower bound:** Let me try $g(x) = \lceil \frac{x^2 + 1}{2} \rceil$. For this to be consistent: $m \geq x^2 - m + 1$ for all x, giving $m \geq \frac{x^2+1}{2}$. For x = 20: $m \geq 200.5$, so $m \geq 201$. I need to find a tenuous function g that minimizes the sum g(1) + g(2) +... + g(20), then determine the minimum possible value of g(14). **Understanding "tenuous":** A function f is tenuous if f(x) + f(y) > x² for all positive integers x and y. **Finding constraints on g:** For any positive integers x and y: $$g(x) + g(y) > x^2$$ Setting y = x: $$g(x) + g(x) > x^2$$ $$2g(x) > x^2$$ $$g(x) > \frac{x^2}{2}$$ Since g is integer-valued: $g(x) \geq \lceil \frac{x^2}{2} \rceil + 1$ or $g(x) \geq \lfloor \frac{x^2}{2} \rfloor + 1$ For integer x: if x² is even, then $g(x) \geq \frac{x^2}{2} + 1$; if x² is odd, then $g(x) \geq \frac{x^2+1}{2}$. This simplifies to: $g(x) \geq \lceil \frac{x^2 + 1}{2} \rceil$ **Checking if we can achieve the lower bound:** Let me try $g(x) = \lceil \frac{x^2 + 1}{2} \rceil$. For even x: $g(x) = \frac{x^2}{2} + 1$ For odd x: $g(x) = \frac{x^2 + 1}{2}$ I need to verify: $g(x) + g(y) > x^2$ for all positive integers x, y. For any x, y: $$g(x) + g(y) \geq \lceil \frac{x^2+1}{2} \rceil + \lceil \frac{y^2+1}{2} \rceil$$ The minimum occurs when both are at their lower bounds. We need: $$\lceil \frac{x^2+1}{2} \rceil + \lceil \frac{y^2+1}{2} \rceil > x^2$$ For x even: $\frac{x^2}{2} + 1 + \lceil \frac{y^2+1}{2} \rceil \geq \frac{x^2}{2} + 1 + 1 = \frac{x^2}{2} + 2 > x^2$ requires $2 > \frac{x^2}{2}$, which fails for x ≥ 3. So we need a larger function. Let me try: $g(x) = \lfloor \frac{x^2}{2} \rfloor + 1$ for all x. For even x: $g(x) = \frac{x^2}{2} + 1$ For odd x: $g(x) = \frac{x^2-1}{2} + 1 = \frac{x^2+1}{2}$ Check: $g(x) + g(y) > x^2$ Worst case is when y is minimized (y=1): - For odd x: $g(x) + g(1) = \frac{x^2+1}{2} + 1 = \frac{x^2+3}{2}$. Need $\frac{x^2+3}{2} > x^2$, so $x^2 + 3 > 2x^2$, giving $3 > x^2$. This fails for x ≥ 2. Let me try $g(x) = \lfloor \frac{x^2}{2} \rfloor + x$: For x=1: $g(1) = 0 + 1 = 1$ For x=2: $g(2) = 2 + 2 = 4$ Check g(2) + g(1) = 4 + 1 = 5 > 4 ✓ After systematic analysis, the minimal tenuous function is: $$g(x) = \lfloor \frac{x^2}{2} \rfloor + x$$ **Computing g(14):** $$g(14) = \lfloor \frac{196}{2} \rfloor + 14 = 98 + 14 = 112$$ Final answer: **112**

Let's denote $f$ as a tenuous function. We need $f(x) + f(y) > x^2$ for all positive integers $x$ and $y$. This means for any positive integer $x$: $f(x) + f(y) > x^2$ for all positive integers $y$. Looking at this problem, I need to understand the constraint on tenuous functions and find how to minimize the sum. ## Understanding the Constraint For a tenuous function $f$: $f(x) + f(y) > x^2$ for all positive integers $x, y$. Let $m = \min\{f(y): y \in \mathbb{Z}^+\}$ be the minimum value of $f$. For any fixed $x$, since this inequality must hold for all $y$: $$m + f(x) > x^2$$ $$f(x) > x^2 - m$$ $$f(x) \geq x^2 - m + 1$$ ## Finding When the Minimum is Achieved Suppose the minimum $m$ is achieved at $x = k$, so $f(k) = m$. Then: $m \geq k^2 - m + 1$ $$2m \geq k^2 + 1$$ $$m \geq \frac{k^2 + 1}{2}$$ For $m$ to be an integer, we need $k$ to be odd. Looking at this problem, I need to understand what the tenuous condition tells us about the structure of $g$. ## Understanding the Tenuous Condition The condition is: $g(x) + g(y) > x^2$ for all positive integers $x$ and $y$. Let $m = \min_z g(z)$ be the minimum value of $g$. Then for any $x$: $$g(x) + m > x^2$$ $$g(x) > x^2 - m$$ Since $g$ is integer-valued: $g(x) \geq x^2 - m + 1$ for all $x$. Also, $g(x) \geq m$ for all $x$ by definition of minimum. Therefore: $$g(x) \geq \max(m, x^2 - m + 1)$$ To minimize $\sum_{i=1}^{20} g(i)$, we should take equality: $$g(x) = \max(m, x^2 - m + 1) \text{ for all } x$$ ## Verifying this is Tenuous For any $x, y$: - If $g(x) = g(y) = m$: then $g(x) + g(y) = 2m > x^2$ (by our constraint) - If $g(x) = x^2 - m + 1, g(y) = m$: then $g(x) + g(y) = x^2 + 1 > x^2$ ✓ - If both $> m$: then $g(x) + g(y) = x^2 - m + 1 + y^2 - m + 1 = x^2 + y^2 - 2m + 2 > x^2$ ✓ This works! We need $2m > x^2$ for all $x$ where $g(x) = m$. ## Finding the Threshold Let $k$ be the largest integer where $k^2 \leq 2m - 1$. Then: - For $i \leq k$: $g(i) = m$ - For $i > k$: $g(i) = i^2 - m + 1$ The sum is: $$S(m) = km + \sum_{i=k+1}^{20}(i^2 - m + 1) = m(2k-20) + \sum_{i=k+1}^{20} i^2 + (20-k)$$ Let me calculate $\sum_{i=1}^{20} i^2 = \frac{20 \cdot 21 \cdot 41}{6} = 2870$ **For $k = 10$:** Need $100 \leq 2m-1 < 121$, so $51 \leq m \leq 60$ $$\sum_{i=11}^{20} i^2 = 2870 - \frac{10 \cdot 11 \cdot 21}{6} = 2870 - 385 = 2485$$ $$S(m) = m(0) + 2485 + 10 = 2495$$ **For $k = 11$:** Need $121 \leq 2m-1 < 144$, so $61 \leq m \leq 72$ $$\sum_{i=12}^{20} i^2 = 2870 - \frac{11 \cdot 12 \cdot 23}{6} = 2870 - 506 = 2364$$ $$S(m) = 2m + 2364 + 9 = 2m + 2373$$ To minimize: $m = 61$ gives $S = 122 + 2373 = 2495$ ✓ **For $k = 9$:** $S(m) = -2m + 2596$, minimum at $m = 50$ gives $S = 2496$ (worse) **For $k = 12$:** $S(m) = 4m + \text{const}$, minimum at $m = 73$ gives $S = 2520$ (worse) The minimum sum of 2495 is achieved only at: - $k = 10, m \in [51, 60]$, or - $k = 11, m = 61$ ## Finding Minimum $g(14)$ For these optimal solutions: **Case $k = 10$:** Since $14 > 10$, $g(14) = 14^2 - m + 1 = 197 - m$ - Maximum $m = 60$ gives minimum $g(14) = 137$ **Case $k = 11$:** Since $14 > 11$, $g(14) = 14^2 - m + 1 = 197 - m$ - With $m = 61$: $g(14) = 197 - 61 = 136$ Final answer: **136**

"""Deterministic verifier — contributor_03 / problem_02.
Tenuous Function Minimal Value. Hand-authored (Claude Code, autonomous; via @yulinl2).
Exact integer final-answer match against the author oracle.
"""

import re
from fractions import Fraction

_MARKERS = [
 r"final\s+answer\s*[:=]?", r"the\s+(?:exact\s+)?answer\s+is\s*[:=]?",
 r"answer\s*[:=]", r"the\s+rate\s+is\s*[:=]?", r"therefore[,:]?",
 r"thus[,:]?", r"hence[,:]?",
]
_MARKER_RE = re.compile("|".join(_MARKERS), re.IGNORECASE)

def _boxed_inner(s):
 """Brace-balanced contents of every \\boxed{...} (handles nested \\frac)."""
 out, i = [], 0
 while True:
 j = s.find("boxed", i)
 if j < 0:
 break
 k = s.find("{", j)
 if k < 0:
 break
 depth, m = 0, k
 while m < len(s):
 if s[m] == "{":
 depth += 1
 elif s[m] == "}":
 depth -= 1
 if depth == 0:
 break
 m += 1
 out.append(s[k + 1:m])
 i = m + 1
 return out

def _normalize(s):
 """LaTeX -> plain so rationals survive: \\frac{a}{b} -> a/b, keep %.
 (c09 fractions are always integer/integer, so the flat a/b form is exact;
 a compound numerator would need parens, not present here.)"""
 # capture an optional leading minus OUTSIDE the frac (-\frac{a}{b} -> -a/b):
 # a detached "-" would otherwise be split off and the component read positive.
 s = re.sub(r"(-?)\s*\\[dt]?frac\s*\{([^{}]*)\}\s*\{([^{}]*)\}", r" \1\2/\3 ", s)
 s = re.sub(r"\\(left|right|!|,|;|:|quad|qquad)", " ", s)
 s = re.sub(r"\\text\s*\{[^{}]*\}", " ", s)
 s = s.replace(r"\%", "%").replace(r"\$", " ").replace("$", " ")
 s = s.replace("{,}", "") # 225{,}000 -> 225000
 s = s.replace("\\", " ").replace("{", " ").replace("}", " ")
 # thousands separator ONLY when strictly adjacent (1,250 -> 1250); never join
 # across a space (a vector's "1907, 379" must stay two numbers).
 s = re.sub(r"(\d),(\d{3})(?!\d)", r"\1\2", s)
 return s

# token: percent | fraction a/b | decimal | integer (left-to-right, non-overlap)
_TOK = re.compile(
 r"(?P<pct>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*%"
 r"|(?P<n>-?\d+)\s*/\s*(?P<d>-?\d+)"
 r"|(?P<dec>-?\d+\.\d+)"
 r"|(?P<int>-?\d+)")

def _rationals(zone):
 """Ordered list of Fraction values committed in `zone` (already a string)."""
 out = []
 for m in _TOK.finditer(_normalize(zone)):
 try:
 if m.group("pct") is not None:
 out.append(Fraction(m.group("pct")) / 100)
 elif m.group("n") is not None:
 d = int(m.group("d"))
 if d == 0:
 continue
 out.append(Fraction(int(m.group("n")), d))
 elif m.group("dec") is not None:
 out.append(Fraction(m.group("dec")))
 else:
 out.append(Fraction(int(m.group("int"))))
 except (ValueError, ZeroDivisionError):
 continue
 return out

def _final_zone(response):
 """The text of the model's committed final answer (most -> least reliable):
 boxed contents; else the last marker line's tail; else the last line."""
 if not response or not response.strip:
 return ""
 boxed = _boxed_inner(response)
 if boxed:
 return " ".join(boxed)
 lines = [ln for ln in response.splitlines if ln.strip]
 # last marker line that actually carries a number (weak discourse markers
 # like "therefore/thus/hence" otherwise hijack the zone to a number-less
 # trailing comment, burying the real commit on the line above).
 for ln in reversed(lines):
 m = _MARKER_RE.search(ln)
 if m and any(c.isdigit for c in ln[m.start:]):
 return ln[m.start:]
 # else the last line that carries a number
 for ln in reversed(lines):
 if any(c.isdigit for c in ln):
 return ln
 return lines[-1] if lines else ""

def _committed_rational(zone):
 """The single COMMITTED final rational in `zone`: the value after the LAST
 '=' if one is present (so an arithmetic line like '105 - 105 = 0' commits 0,
 NOT the intermediate 105 — the loose 'oracle appears anywhere' false-positive
 the cold-read found), else the last rational. Returns (value|None, all)."""
 cands = _rationals(zone)
 if not cands:
 return None, []
 norm = _normalize(zone)
 if "=" in norm:
 tail = _rationals(norm.rsplit("=", 1)[1])
 if tail:
 return tail[-1], cands
 # no '=': the committed value is the FIRST rational (right after the marker /
 # at the head of the line) — a trailing parenthetical like "0 (note 105)" or
 # "253 (> 200)" must not steal the verdict.
 return cands[0], cands

def match_exact(response, oracle):
 """oracle: Fraction. The COMMITTED final must equal it EXACTLY (no tolerance
 — rounded-only decimals are insufficient per the gradingscheme). Grades the
 committed value, not any number in the zone (no substring/intermediate pass)."""
 committed, cands = _committed_rational(_final_zone(response))
 if committed is None:
 return False, "no rational final answer could be extracted"
 if committed == oracle:
 return True, "committed %s == oracle %s" % (committed, oracle)
 return False, "committed %s != oracle %s (cands %s)" % (
 committed, oracle, [str(c) for c in cands])

def match_vector(response, oracle):
 """oracle: list[Fraction]. Every component must appear in the final zone."""
 cands = set(_rationals(_final_zone(response)))
 missing = [str(o) for o in oracle if o not in cands]
 if not missing:
 return True, "all %d components present" % len(oracle)
 return False, "missing/incorrect components: %s" % missing

def match_rate(response, oracle):
 """oracle: Fraction rate (e.g. 39/125). Accept the exact fraction, the
 decimal (tol 1e-4, the percent form is inherently rounded), or the percent
 (bare integer like 31.2 read as 31.2%)."""
 committed, cands = _committed_rational(_final_zone(response))
 if committed is None:
 return False, "no rational final answer could be extracted"
 r = oracle
 rf = float(r)
 cf = float(committed)
 if committed == r:
 return True, "exact %s == oracle %s" % (committed, r)
 if abs(cf - rf) < 1e-4:
 return True, "decimal %s ~= oracle %s" % (committed, r)
 if abs(cf - rf * 100) < 1e-2:
 return True, "percent %s ~= oracle %s%%" % (committed, float(r * 100))
 return False, "committed %s != oracle %s (=%.6g; cands %s)" % (
 committed, r, rf, [str(c) for c in cands])


def grade(response: str, context: dict) -> dict:
 """Tenuous Function Minimal Value

 Oracle: Fraction(136) (author answerkey; frontier-sweep consensus matches). Exact
 integer final-answer match — intermediate numbers in the derivation are
 ignored (only the committed final zone is graded)."""
 ok, reason = match_exact(response, Fraction(136))
 return {"pass": bool(ok), "score": 1.0 if ok else 0.0, "notes": reason}

 out = grade(response=data['response'], context=data['context'])
 print(json.dumps(out))

💭 What's promising
  • The reference solution is clean and (modulo the contamination concern) correct: the $g(x)\ge\max(m, x^2+1-m)$ envelope and the discrete optimization over m are handled carefully.
  • Single-integer deliverable (136) is a perfect exact-match verifier target.
  • Nice touch catching the boundary case at m=61 where S(61)=S(60)=2495 — shows the optimum is a plateau, which is the part solvers most often get wrong.
❓ Open questions to think through
  • This is HMMT February 2010 (Team Round) almost verbatim — the term 'tenuous', the 1..20 sum, and the g(14) ask are the original wording. Frontier models very likely have this memorized, so a pass would measure recall, not reasoning.
  • The sidecar is still the untouched template — no sample responses, so we can't yet confirm the problem stumps frontier models, and if it's contaminated we'd expect it NOT to.
  • Minor statement nit: 'for all positive integers x and y' with the bound depending only on x means the y-quantifier just forces $g(y)\ge$ the global-min term — fine, but a solver may pause on the asymmetry. The solution relies on this exact reading.
🌱 Directions to explore
  • Strongly consider re-skinning to defeat memorization: change the threshold ($x^2 \to x^2+c$ or a non-square), the sum range (1..20), and the query index (g(14)) together, then re-derive the answer. A fresh numeric target is what makes this benchmark-useful.
  • Run 3 independent frontier samples and paste them in the sidecar — if they all nail 136 verbatim, that's direct evidence of contamination and a signal to reskin.
